When save_for_backward=True, saves dot/gate_score/rstd_x/rstd_k for backward.\"\"\"\n    num_tokens = T.dynamic('num_tokens')\n    threads = 32\n    vec_size = 8\n\n    # NOTE Performance only tuned for hidden_size in {4096, 7168}\n    def _choose_blk_d(hidden_size):\n        for blk in [1024, 768, 512, 256]:\n            if hidden_size % blk == 0 and hidden_size >= 2 * blk:\n                return blk\n        raise ValueError(f'No valid blk_d for hidden_size={hidden_size}')\n\n    def _choose_num_persistent_blocks(hidden_size, blk_d, num_sms, hc_mult):\n        \"\"\"Estimate from SM shared memory occupancy, capped by register pressure.\"\"\"\n        # smem per block: x_smem (bf16) + kv_smem double-buffer (bf16)\n        smem_bytes = hidden_size * 2 + blk_d * 4\n        blocks_per_sm = min(get_max_smem_per_sm() // smem_bytes, 16)  # 16: register pressure cap\n        return num_sms * blocks_per_sm // hc_mult\n\n    blk_d = _choose_blk_d(hidden_size)\n    num_persistent_blocks = _choose_num_persistent_blocks(hidden_size, blk_d, num_sms, hc_mult)\n\n    assert hidden_size % blk_d == 0\n    assert hidden_size >= 2 * blk_d\n    num_blk = hidden_size // blk_d\n    reduce_blk = threads * vec_size\n    sub_blks = blk_d // reduce_blk\n    v_start_phase = num_blk % 2\n\n    @T.prim_func\n    def engram_gate_fwd_kernel(\n        hidden_states: T.Tensor[(num_tokens, hc_mult, hidden_size), T.bfloat16],\n        k: T.StridedTensor[(num_tokens, hc_mult, hidden_size), (k_stride_s, k_stride_h, 1), T.bfloat16],\n        v: T.StridedTensor[(num_tokens, hidden_size), (v_stride_s, 1), T.bfloat16],\n        weight_fused: T.Tensor[(hc_mult, hidden_size), T.float],\n        output: T.Tensor[(num_tokens, hc_mult, hidden_size), T.bfloat16],\n        dot_out: T.Tensor[(num_tokens, hc_mult), T.float],\n        gate_score: T.Tensor[(num_tokens, hc_mult), T.float],\n        rstd_x: T.Tensor[(num_tokens, hc_mult), T.float],\n        rstd_k: T.Tensor[(num_tokens, hc_mult), T.float],\n    ):\n        with T.Kernel(hc_mult, num_persistent_blocks, threads=threads) as (pid_h, pid_b):\n            thread_idx = T.get_thread_binding()\n            x_local = T.alloc_local((vec_size,), T.float)\n            k_local = T.alloc_local((vec_size,), T.float)\n            w_local = T.alloc_local((vec_size,), T.float)\n            v_local = T.alloc_local((vec_size,), T.float)\n            gate_score_local = T.alloc_local((1,), T.float)\n            rstd_x_local = T.alloc_local((1,), T.float)\n            rstd_k_local = T.alloc_local((1,), T.float)\n            gate_score_reducer = T.alloc_local((1,), T.float)\n            rstd_x_reducer = T.alloc_local((1,), T.float)\n            rstd_k_reducer = T.alloc_local((1,), T.float)\n\n            x_smem = T.alloc_shared((hidden_size,), T.bfloat16)\n            kv_smem = T.alloc_shared((2, blk_d), T.bfloat16)\n\n            per_block = T.ceildiv(num_tokens, num_persistent_blocks)\n            t_start = T.min(per_block * pid_b, num_tokens)\n            t_end = T.min(per_block * (pid_b + 1), num_tokens)\n\n            for i_s in T.Serial(t_start, t_end):\n                # === Pass 1: Reduction with cp.async pipeline ===\n                if i_s == t_start:\n                    T.async_copy(hidden_states[i_s, pid_h, 0:blk_d], x_smem[0:blk_d])\n                    T.async_copy(k[i_s, pid_h, 0:blk_d], kv_smem[0, :])\n\n                T.clear(rstd_k_local)\n                T.clear(rstd_x_local)\n                T.clear(gate_score_local)\n\n                for i_b in T.Serial(1, num_blk):\n                    phase = i_b % 2\n                    prev_phase = (i_b - 1) % 2\n                    T.async_copy(hidden_states[i_s, pid_h, i_b * blk_d:(i_b + 1) * blk_d], x_smem[i_b * blk_d:(i_b + 1) * blk_d])\n                    T.async_copy(k[i_s, pid_h, i_b * blk_d:(i_b + 1) * blk_d], kv_smem[phase, :])\n                    T.ptx_wait_group(2)\n                    for i_sub in T.Serial(sub_blks):\n                        sub_base = (i_b - 1) * blk_d + i_sub * reduce_blk\n                        for i_k in T.vectorized(vec_size):\n                            x_local[i_k] = x_smem[sub_base + thread_idx * vec_size + i_k]\n                            k_local[i_k] = kv_smem[prev_phase, i_sub * reduce_blk + thread_idx * vec_size + i_k]\n                        for i_k in T.vectorized(vec_size):\n                            w_local[i_k] = weight_fused[pid_h, sub_base + thread_idx * vec_size + i_k]\n                        for i_k in T.serial(vec_size):\n                            rstd_x_local[0] += x_local[i_k] * x_local[i_k]\n                            rstd_k_local[0] += k_local[i_k] * k_local[i_k]\n                            gate_score_local[0] += x_local[i_k] * w_local[i_k] * k_local[i_k]\n\n                # Epilogue: process last tile\n                T.ptx_wait_group(0)\n\n                # Prefetch v[0] into freed kv_smem bank\n                T.async_copy(v[i_s, 0:blk_d], kv_smem[v_start_phase, :])\n\n                for i_sub in T.Serial(sub_blks):\n                    sub_base = (num_blk - 1) * blk_d + i_sub * reduce_blk\n                    for i_k in T.vectorized(vec_size):\n                        x_local[i_k] = x_smem[sub_base + thread_idx * vec_size + i_k]\n                        k_local[i_k] = kv_smem[(num_blk - 1) % 2, i_sub * reduce_blk + thread_idx * vec_size + i_k]\n                    for i_k in T.vectorized(vec_size):\n                        w_local[i_k] = weight_fused[pid_h, sub_base + thread_idx * vec_size + i_k]\n                    for i_k in T.serial(vec_size):\n                        rstd_x_local[0] += x_local[i_k] * x_local[i_k]\n                        rstd_k_local[0] += k_local[i_k] * k_local[i_k]\n                        gate_score_local[0] += x_local[i_k] * w_local[i_k] * k_local[i_k]\n\n                # Prefetch v[1]\n                T.async_copy(v[i_s, blk_d:2 * blk_d], kv_smem[1 - v_start_phase, :])\n\n                rstd_k_reducer[0] = T.warp_reduce_sum(rstd_k_local[0])\n                rstd_x_reducer[0] = T.warp_reduce_sum(rstd_x_local[0])\n                gate_score_reducer[0] = T.warp_reduce_sum(gate_score_local[0])\n\n                rstd_x_reducer[0] = T.rsqrt(rstd_x_reducer[0] / hidden_size + eps)\n                rstd_k_reducer[0] = T.rsqrt(rstd_k_reducer[0] / hidden_size + eps)\n\n                if save_for_backward:\n                    if thread_idx == 0:\n                        dot_out[i_s, pid_h] = gate_score_reducer[0]\n                        rstd_x[i_s, pid_h] = rstd_x_reducer[0]\n                        rstd_k[i_s, pid_h] = rstd_k_reducer[0]\n\n                gate_score_reducer[0] = gate_score_reducer[0] * rstd_x_reducer[0] * rstd_k_reducer[0] * scalar\n\n                gate_score_reducer[0] = T.sigmoid(T.copysign(T.sqrt(T.clamp(T.abs(gate_score_reducer[0]), clamp_value, float('inf'))), gate_score_reducer[0]))\n\n                if save_for_backward:\n                    if thread_idx == 0:\n                        gate_score[i_s, pid_h] = gate_score_reducer[0]\n\n                # === Pass 2: Output — x from smem, v from kv_smem (tiles 0,1 already prefetched) ===\n                for i_b in T.Serial(num_blk):\n                    tile_phase = (v_start_phase + i_b) % 2\n                    if i_b < num_blk - 1:\n                        T.ptx_wait_group(1)\n                    else:\n                        T.ptx_wait_group(0)\n                        # Prefetch next token's k and x\n                        if i_s + 1 < t_end:\n                            T.async_copy(k[i_s + 1, pid_h, 0:blk_d], kv_smem[0, :])\n                            T.async_copy(hidden_states[i_s + 1, pid_h, 0:blk_d], x_smem[0:blk_d])\n                    for i_sub in T.Serial(sub_blks):\n                        sub_base = i_b * blk_d + i_sub * reduce_blk\n                        for i_k in T.vectorized(vec_size):\n                            x_local[i_k] = x_smem[sub_base + thread_idx * vec_size + i_k]\n                            v_local[i_k] = kv_smem[tile_phase, i_sub * reduce_blk + thread_idx * vec_size + i_k]\n                        for i_k in T.vectorized(vec_size):\n                            output[i_s, pid_h, sub_base + thread_idx * vec_size + i_k] = x_local[i_k] + gate_score_reducer[0] * v_local[i_k]\n                    # Prefetch v[i_b+2] into freed kv_smem bank\n                    if i_b + 2 < num_blk:\n                        T.async_copy(v[i_s, (i_b + 2) * blk_d:(i_b + 3) * blk_d], kv_smem[tile_phase, :])\n\n    return engram_gate_fwd_kernel\n\n\n@tilelang.jit(\n    pass_configs={\n        tilelang.PassConfigKey.TL_DISABLE_WARP_SPECIALIZED: True,\n        tilelang.PassConfigKey.TL_DISABLE_THREAD_STORAGE_SYNC: True,\n        tilelang.PassConfigKey.TL_DISABLE_OUT_OF_BOUND_WARNING: True,\n    },\n)\ndef get_engram_gate_bwd_kernel(\n    hidden_size: int,\n    scalar: float,\n    k_stride_s: int,\n    k_stride_h: int,\n    v_stride_s: int,\n    num_persistent_blocks: int,\n    clamp_value: float = 1e-6,\n    hc_mult: int = 4,\n):\n    \"\"\"Backward kernel: 8 warps per CTA, 2 warps per head.\n\n    grad_out and v cached in shared memory. grad_w accumulates in registers.\n    Cross-warp dldg reduction via shared memory.\n    \"\"\"\n    assert hc_mult == 4\n    num_tokens = T.dynamic('num_tokens')\n    warp_size = 32\n    warps_per_head = 2\n    num_warps = hc_mult * warps_per_head\n    threads = warp_size * num_warps\n    threads_per_head = warp_size * warps_per_head\n    assert hidden_size % threads == 0\n    elems_per_thread = hidden_size // threads\n    elems_per_warp_pair = hidden_size // threads_per_head\n    go_vec_size = 8\n    x_vec_size = 4\n\n    # NOTE Performance only tuned for hidden_size in {4096, 7168}\n    def _choose_v_vec_size(elems_per_thread):\n        for vec in [4, 2, 1]:\n            if elems_per_thread % vec == 0:\n                return vec\n\n    def _choose_go_blk_d(hidden_size, go_tile):\n        \"\"\"Largest multiple of go_tile that divides hidden_size, with >= 2 tiles.\"\"\"\n        result = go_tile\n        for blk in range(go_tile, hidden_size // 2 + 1, go_tile):\n            if hidden_size % blk == 0:\n                result = blk\n        return result\n\n    def _choose_x_blk_d(hidden_size, x_tile, hc_mult, warps_per_head):\n        \"\"\"Largest multiple of x_tile that divides hidden_size, <= hidden_size // 2, fits in smem.\"\"\"\n        smem_fixed = (hc_mult + 1) * hidden_size * 2 + hc_mult * warps_per_head * 4\n        smem_per_x = 2 * hc_mult * (2 + 2 + 4)\n        x_smem_limit = (get_max_smem_per_sm() - smem_fixed) // smem_per_x\n        x_limit = min(x_smem_limit, hidden_size // 2)\n        result = x_tile\n        for blk in range(x_tile, x_limit + 1, x_tile):\n            if hidden_size % blk == 0:\n                result = blk\n        return result\n\n    v_vec_size = _choose_v_vec_size(elems_per_thread)\n    go_blk_d = _choose_go_blk_d(hidden_size, threads_per_head * go_vec_size)\n    x_blk_d = _choose_x_blk_d(hidden_size, threads_per_head * x_vec_size, hc_mult, warps_per_head)\n\n    assert hidden_size % go_blk_d == 0 and hidden_size % x_blk_d == 0\n    assert go_blk_d % (threads_per_head * go_vec_size) == 0\n    assert x_blk_d % (threads_per_head * x_vec_size) == 0\n    assert go_blk_d + x_blk_d <= hidden_size\n\n    def smem_layout(i, j, vs):\n        thread_id = i * threads_per_head + (j // vs) % threads_per_head\n        local_id = (j % vs) + (j // (threads_per_head * vs)) * vs\n        return thread_id, local_id\n\n    @T.prim_func\n    def engram_gate_bwd_kernel(\n        grad_out: T.Tensor[(num_tokens, hc_mult, hidden_size), T.bfloat16],\n        hidden_states: T.Tensor[(num_tokens, hc_mult, hidden_size), T.bfloat16],\n        k: T.StridedTensor[(num_tokens, hc_mult, hidden_size), (k_stride_s, k_stride_h, 1), T.bfloat16],\n        v: T.StridedTensor[(num_tokens, hidden_size), (v_stride_s, 1), T.bfloat16],\n        weight_fused: T.Tensor[(hc_mult, hidden_size), T.float],\n        dot_in: T.Tensor[(num_tokens, hc_mult), T.float],\n        gate_in: T.Tensor[(num_tokens, hc_mult), T.float],\n        rstd_x_in: T.Tensor[(num_tokens, hc_mult), T.float],\n        rstd_k_in: T.Tensor[(num_tokens, hc_mult), T.float],\n        grad_x: T.Tensor[(num_tokens, hc_mult, hidden_size), T.bfloat16],\n        grad_k: T.Tensor[(num_tokens, hc_mult, hidden_size), T.bfloat16],\n        grad_v: T.Tensor[(num_tokens, hidden_size), T.bfloat16],\n        grad_w_partial: T.Tensor[(num_persistent_blocks, hc_mult, hidden_size), T.float],\n    ):\n        with T.Kernel(num_persistent_blocks, threads=threads) as pid_p:\n            tid = T.get_thread_binding()\n            warp_id = T.get_warp_idx()\n            lane_id = T.get_lane_idx()\n            head_id = warp_id // warps_per_head\n            sub_warp_id = warp_id % warps_per_head\n\n            go_local = T.alloc_local((go_vec_size,), T.float)\n            v_local = T.alloc_local((go_vec_size,), T.float)\n            go_v_local = T.alloc_local((v_vec_size,), T.float)\n            go_x_local = T.alloc_local((x_vec_size,), T.float)\n            x_local = T.alloc_local((x_vec_size,), T.float)\n            k_local = T.alloc_local((x_vec_size,), T.float)\n            w_fused_local = T.alloc_local((x_vec_size,), T.float)\n            grad_v_partial = T.alloc_local((v_vec_size,), T.float)\n            grad_w_local = T.alloc_local((elems_per_warp_pair,), T.float)\n\n            dldg_local = T.alloc_local((1,), T.float)\n            dldg_r = T.alloc_local((1,), T.float)\n\n            gate_local = T.alloc_local((hc_mult,), T.float)\n            gate_local_hc = T.alloc_var(T.float)\n            rstd_x_local = T.alloc_var(T.float)\n            rstd_k_local = T.alloc_var(T.float)\n            dot_in_local = T.alloc_var(T.float)\n            dot_x_local = T.alloc_var(T.float)\n            dot_k_local = T.alloc_var(T.float)\n\n            go_copy_layout = T.Fragment((hc_mult, go_blk_d), forward_fn=partial(smem_layout, vs=go_vec_size))\n            x_copy_layout = T.Fragment((hc_mult, x_blk_d), forward_fn=partial(smem_layout, vs=x_vec_size))\n\n            go_smem = T.alloc_shared((hc_mult, hidden_size), T.bfloat16)\n            v_smem = T.alloc_shared((hidden_size,), T.bfloat16)\n            x_smem = T.alloc_shared((2, hc_mult, x_blk_d), T.bfloat16)\n            k_smem = T.alloc_shared((2, hc_mult, x_blk_d), T.bfloat16)\n            w_smem = T.alloc_shared((2, hc_mult, x_blk_d), T.float)\n            dldg_smem = T.alloc_shared((hc_mult, warps_per_head), T.float)\n\n            per_block = T.ceildiv(num_tokens, num_persistent_blocks)\n            t_start = T.min(per_block * pid_p, num_tokens)\n            t_end = T.min(per_block * (pid_p + 1), num_tokens)\n\n            T.clear(grad_w_local)\n\n            for i_s in T.serial(t_start, t_end):\n                # === Prologue: load grad_out and v into smem ===\n                if i_s == t_start:\n                    T.async_copy(v[i_s, :], v_smem)\n                    T.async_copy(grad_out[i_s, :, :go_blk_d], go_smem[:, :go_blk_d], loop_layout=go_copy_layout)\n                    T.ptx_wait_group(1)\n                    # ensure v_smem is readable by all threads\n                    T.sync_threads()\n\n                T.copy(gate_in[i_s, :], gate_local)\n\n                # Per-head scalar loads\n                gate_local_hc = gate_in[i_s, head_id]\n                rstd_x_local = rstd_x_in[i_s, head_id]\n                rstd_k_local = rstd_k_in[i_s, head_id]\n                dot_in_local = dot_in[i_s, head_id]\n\n                T.clear(dldg_local)\n\n                go_sub_blks = go_blk_d // (threads_per_head * go_vec_size)\n                num_go_tiles = hidden_size // go_blk_d\n\n                # === Pass 1a: dldg — two warps per head ===\n                for i_b in T.serial(1, num_go_tiles):\n                    T.async_copy(grad_out[i_s, :, i_b * go_blk_d:(i_b + 1) * go_blk_d],\n                                 go_smem[:, i_b * go_blk_d:(i_b + 1) * go_blk_d],\n                                 loop_layout=go_copy_layout)\n                    T.ptx_wait_group(1)\n                    for i_sub in T.serial(go_sub_blks):\n                        go_base = (i_b - 1) * go_blk_d + i_sub * threads_per_head * go_vec_size + sub_warp_id * warp_size * go_vec_size\n                        for i_k in T.vectorized(go_vec_size):\n                            go_local[i_k] = go_smem[head_id, go_base + lane_id * go_vec_size + i_k]\n                            v_local[i_k] = v_smem[go_base + lane_id * go_vec_size + i_k]\n                        for i_k in T.serial(go_vec_size):\n                            dldg_local[0] += go_local[i_k] * v_local[i_k]\n\n                # Epilogue: process last go tile\n                T.ptx_wait_group(0)\n                for i_sub in T.serial(go_sub_blks):\n                    go_base = (num_go_tiles - 1) * go_blk_d + i_sub * threads_per_head * go_vec_size + sub_warp_id * warp_size * go_vec_size\n                    for i_k in T.vectorized(go_vec_size):\n                        go_local[i_k] = go_smem[head_id, go_base + lane_id * go_vec_size + i_k]\n                        v_local[i_k] = v_smem[go_base + lane_id * go_vec_size + i_k]\n                    for i_k in T.serial(go_vec_size):\n                        dldg_local[0] += go_local[i_k] * v_local[i_k]\n\n                # Cross-warp dldg reduction via smem\n                dldg_local[0] = T.warp_reduce_sum(dldg_local[0])\n                if lane_id == 0:\n                    dldg_smem[head_id, sub_warp_id] = dldg_local[0]\n                T.sync_threads()\n\n                # Prefetch next token's v\n                if i_s + 1 < t_end:\n                    T.async_copy(v[i_s + 1, :], v_smem)\n\n                T.async_copy(hidden_states[i_s, :, :x_blk_d], x_smem[0, :, :], loop_layout=x_copy_layout)\n                T.async_copy(k[i_s, :, :x_blk_d], k_smem[0, :, :], loop_layout=x_copy_layout)\n                T.async_copy(weight_fused[:, :x_blk_d], w_smem[0, :, :], loop_layout=x_copy_layout)\n\n                # Gate derivative\n                dldg_r[0] = dldg_smem[head_id, 0] + dldg_smem[head_id, 1]\n                dldg_r[0] = T.Select(\n                    T.abs(dot_in_local) * scalar * rstd_x_local * rstd_k_local < clamp_value,\n                    0.0,\n                    dldg_r[0] * gate_local_hc * (1.0 - gate_local_hc) * 0.5 * T.sqrt(scalar * rstd_x_local * rstd_k_local / T.abs(dot_in_local))\n                )\n\n                # === Pass 1b: grad_v ===\n                for i in T.serial(elems_per_thread // v_vec_size):\n                    T.clear(grad_v_partial)\n                    for i_h in T.unroll(hc_mult):\n                        for i_k in T.vectorized(v_vec_size):\n                            go_v_local[i_k] = go_smem[i_h, i * threads * v_vec_size + tid * v_vec_size + i_k]\n                        for i_k in T.vectorized(v_vec_size):\n                            grad_v_partial[i_k] += go_v_local[i_k] * gate_local[i_h]\n                    for i_k in T.vectorized(v_vec_size):\n                        grad_v[i_s, i * threads * v_vec_size + tid * v_vec_size + i_k] = grad_v_partial[i_k]\n\n                dot_x_local = dot_in_local * rstd_x_local * rstd_x_local / hidden_size\n                dot_k_local = dot_in_local * rstd_k_local * rstd_k_local / hidden_size\n\n                # === Pass 2: grad_x, grad_k, grad_w — pipelined x/k, 2 warps per head ===\n                x_sub_blks = x_blk_d // (threads_per_head * x_vec_size)\n                num_x_tiles = hidden_size // x_blk_d\n\n                for i_b in T.unroll(1, num_x_tiles):\n                    phase = i_b % 2\n                    prev = (i_b - 1) % 2\n\n                    T.async_copy(hidden_states[i_s, :, i_b * x_blk_d:(i_b + 1) * x_blk_d],\n                                 x_smem[phase, :, :], loop_layout=x_copy_layout)\n                    T.async_copy(k[i_s, :, i_b * x_blk_d:(i_b + 1) * x_blk_d],\n                                 k_smem[phase, :, :], loop_layout=x_copy_layout)\n                    T.async_copy(weight_fused[:, i_b * x_blk_d:(i_b + 1) * x_blk_d],\n                                 w_smem[phase, :, :], loop_layout=x_copy_layout)\n\n                    T.ptx_wait_group(3)\n\n                    for i_sub in T.unroll(x_sub_blks):\n                        sub_off = i_sub * (threads_per_head * x_vec_size) + sub_warp_id * (warp_size * x_vec_size)\n                        global_base = (i_b - 1) * x_blk_d + sub_off\n                        reg_base = ((i_b - 1) * x_sub_blks + i_sub) * x_vec_size\n                        for i_k in T.vectorized(x_vec_size):\n                            go_x_local[i_k] = {"type":"reasoning","timestamp":1784399132393,"sessionID":"ses_0898705fcffegJNur44rk0jIRi","part":{"id":"prt_f7679a736001ou4yK3MOLpy9Sd","messageID":"msg_f76799e5d001hu44s4fmpy6TXO","sessionID":"ses_0898705fcffegJNur44rk0jIRi","type":"reasoning","text":"Let me understand the operation deeply first:\n\nPer (token, head):\n- `rstd_x = rsqrt(mean(x^2, dim=-1) + eps)`\n- `rstd_k = rsqrt(mean(k^2, dim=-1) + eps)`\n- `raw_dot = sum(x * k * weight_fused, dim=-1)`\n- `dot = raw_dot * rstd_x * rstd_k * hidden_size**-0.5`\n- `gate_score = sigmoid(sign(dot) * sqrt(clamp_min(abs(dot), clamp_value)))`\n- `out = (x + gate_score * v).bfloat16()`\n\nThe TileLang kernel:\n- Per persistent block processing a range of tokens\n- Uses cp.async for memory loads\n- Shared memory: x_smem (hidden_size bf16), kv_smem (2 * blk_d bf16)\n- First pass: compute rstd_x, rstd_k, raw_dot via reduction\n- Second pass: compute output using x from smem and v from kv_smem\n\nKey constraints for Triton on MI350 (AMD):\n- We want coalesced memory access\n- Vectorized loads (using block sizes that are multiples of 8 for bf16)\n- Good occupancy\n- This is memory-bandwidth-bound, so minimizing memory traffic is key\n\nLet me think about the Triton kernel design:\n- We can launch one block per (token, head) pair, or process multiple tokens/heads per block\n- For hidden_size=4096 and num_tokens=8192, hc_mult=4: total 32768 (token, head) pairs\n- Each block needs to read x (4096 bf16 = 8KB), k (8KB), v (4096 bf16 = 8KB, but shared across heads), weight_fused (4096 f32 = 16KB, can be cached)\n- Actually v is (num_tokens, hidden_size), each head in same token reads the same v\n- Output: write 8KB per (token, head)\n\nTotal memory traffic per (token, head):\n- Read x: 8KB\n- Read k: 8KB\n- Read v: 8KB (but amortized over hc_mult heads if we process all heads of same token together)\n- Read weight_fused: 16KB (but cached/reused heavily)\n- Write output: 8KB\n- Write intermediates (save_for_backward=True): dot (4B), gate_score (4B), rstd_x (4B), rstd_k (4B) = 16B\n\nIf we process 1 head per block, total memory per block: x + k + v + weight_fused + output + intermediates\n\nIf we process multiple heads together (e.g., all 4 heads of one token in a block), we save v reads.\n\nBut Triton works well with 1D blocks for reduction. Let me think about a 2D grid:\n- Block dimension: process a chunk of hidden_size per thread\n- Grid: (num_tokens, hc_mult) 1D or 2D\n\nFor hidden_size=4096, if we use 256 threads per block and each thread processes 16 elements (vec_size=8, so 8 elements per vectorized load, 2 iterations), that's 4096 elements.\n\nActually, the standard Triton approach for reduction:\n```python\n@triton.jit\ndef kernel(...,\n    BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,\n):\n    pid_token = tl.program_id(0)\n    pid_head = tl.program_id(1)\n    \n    # Compute offsets\n    base = (pid_token * stride_x_s + pid_head * stride_x_h)\n    \n    # Accumulators\n    sum_x2 = 0.0\n    sum_k2 = 0.0\n    sum_xkw = 0.0\n    \n    # Loop over hidden_size in chunks of BLOCK_SIZE\n    for off in range(0, HIDDEN_SIZE, BLOCK_SIZE):\n        offsets = off + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)\n        mask = offsets < HIDDEN_SIZE\n        \n        x = tl.load(x_ptr + base + offsets, mask=mask).to(tl.float32)\n        k = tl.load(k_ptr + base + offsets, mask=mask).to(tl.float32)\n        w = tl.load(w_ptr + pid_head * hidden_size + offsets, mask=mask)\n        \n        sum_x2 += tl.sum(x * x)\n        sum_k2 += tl.sum(k * k)\n        sum_xkw += tl.sum(x * k * w)\n```\n\nBut this loads `w` every time. We can load `w` once and keep in registers, but weight_fused is 16KB per head (4096 * 4 bytes). Let me estimate:\n- Grid of maybe 1024 blocks (to get good occupancy)\n- Each block loops over ~32 instances\n\nActually, for AMD, we might want more blocks to hide latency. Reduction over hidden_size\n        sum_x2 = 0.0\n        sum_k2 = 0.0\n        sum_dot = 0.0\n        \n        for d_start in range(0, hidden_size, BLOCK_D):\n            offs_d = d_start + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D)\n            mask = offs_d < hidden_size\n            \n            x_ptrs = hidden_states_ptr + t_idx * stride_xt + h_idx * stride_xh + offs_d * stride_xd\n            k_ptrs = k_ptr + t_idx * stride_kt + h_idx * stride_kh + offs_d * stride_kd\n            w_ptrs = weight_fused_ptr + h_idx * stride_wt + offs_d * stride_wd\n            \n            x = tl.load(x_ptrs, mask=mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)\n            k = tl.load(k_ptrs, mask=mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)\n            w = tl.load(w_ptrs, mask=mask, other=0.0)\n            \n            sum_x2 += tl.sum(x * x, axis=0)\n            sum_k2 += tl.sum(k * k, axis=0)\n            sum_dot += tl.sum(x * k * w, axis=0)\n        \n        rstd_x_val = tl.rsqrt(sum_x2 / hidden_size + eps)\n        rstd_k_val = tl.rsqrt(sum_k2 / hidden_size + eps)\n        \n        dot_val = sum_dot * rstd_x_val * rstd_k_val * scalar\n        signed_sqrt = tl.copysign(tl.sqrt(tl.maximum(tl.abs(dot_val), clamp_value)), dot_val)\n        gate = tl.sigmoid(signed_sqrt)\n        \n        if save_for_backward:\n            if tl.num_programs(0) == 1 or True:  # Only one thread writes\n                # Need to ensure only one thread writes\n                pass\n```\n\nWait, the issue is that `tl.sum` across axis=0 is a block-level reduction. But with mask, the masked-out elements should be 0.0. Good.\n\nBut the writes to scalar outputs (dot, gate, rstd) should only be done by one thread in the block. In Triton, we can do:\n```python\ntl.store(dot_ptr + t_idx * hc_mult + h_idx, sum_dot)\n```\nBut `dot_ptr` is a 1D pointer to scalar values. Or we can use `tl.store` with a mask on the thread ID.\n\nActually, in Triton, when the address is the same for all threads, there's typically hardware support for reducing/serializing stores, but it's better to explicitly use one thread.\n\nNow for the output write:\n```python\nfor d_start in range(0, hidden_size, BLOCK_D):\n    offs_d = d_start + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D)\n    mask = offs_d < hidden_size\n    x_ptrs = ...\n    v_ptrs = v_ptr + t_idx * stride_vt + offs_d * stride_vd\n    o_ptrs = output_ptr + ...\n    \n    x = tl.load(x_ptrs, mask=mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)\n    v = tl.load(v_ptrs, mask=mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)\n    out = x + gate * v\n    tl.store(o_ptrs, out.to(tl.bfloat16), mask=mask)\n```\n\nThis reads x twice (once during reduction, once during output). That's extra memory traffic. \n\nTotal read traffic with this approach:\n- Reduce: x, k, w\n- Output: x, v\nTotal: 2x + k + v + w = 4096*2 + 4096 + 4096 + 4096*2 = 20480 bytes per head per token in bf16, plus w in fp32\n\nWait, w is fp32, but we only read it once during reduction. \n\nActually, in bf16:\n- x: 8192 bytes\n- k: 8192 bytes\n- v: 8192 bytes\n- w: 16384 bytes (fp32)\nTotal reads: 32768 bytes + 16384 = 49152 bytes per instance\n\nPlus output write: 8192 bytes\n\nTotal traffic: ~57KB per instance * 32768 instances = ~1.8 GB\n\nWait, but for num_tokens=8192, hc_mult=4, total_instances=32768. Each instance handles 4096 hidden dim.\nx per instance: 8192 bytes (bf16)\nTotal x memory: 8192 * 32768 = 256 MB. Yes.\n\nMy estimated traffic:\nReads: x(256MB) + k(256MB) + v(64MB) + w(64KB)\nWrites: out(256MB) + dot/gate/rstd_x/rstd_k (~1MB)\n\nPlus reading x and v again for output: wait, if we read x twice, that's another 256MB.\n\nTotal: 256+256+64 + 256 = 832 MB read, 256 MB write = 1088 MB total\nAt 5.3 TB/s: 0.205 ms\n\nIf we can cache x in shared memory or registers between reduction and output, we save 256MB of reads.\n\nWith BLOCK_D = 4096: we can load x into registers and reuse. But 4096 bf16 elements = 8192 bytes. With 256 threads, each thread holds 32 bf16 = 64 bytes in registers. That's very manageable.\n\nActually, with Triton, if we load x during reduction and keep it, we can reuse. Yes, if we use `tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D)` and BLOCK_D is a constexpr. Triton should tile this automatically if needed, or generate one big block. Actually, with 256 threads and BLOCK_D=4096, Triton will vectorize the loads.\n\nThe issue with very large BLOCK_D is that the mask doesn't apply (since hidden_size is exactly 4096), so it's fine.\n\nBut with BLOCK_D=4096 and 256 threads, each thread processes 16 elements. The generated code should use 8-wide vector loads (128-bit), so 2 loads per thread.\n\nNow, for the persistent kernel on AMD, how many programs should we launch?\n\nWe can try num_programs = num_tokens * hc_mult (32768). But AMD MI350 has 256 CUs. Launching 32768 blocks is fine - the hardware will serialize them. But this means no persistent loop.\n\nAlternatively, we can launch fewer blocks and do a persistent loop:\n```python\nnum_programs = something like 2048 or 4096\nfor idx in range(pid, total, num_programs):\n    ...\n```\n\nPersistent kernels can be faster because they amortize block launch overhead and potentially improve cache locality. But on AMD, block launch overhead might be different.\n\nFor a memory bandwidth bound kernel, what's most important is:\n1. Vectorized loads\n2. Coalesced access\n3. But within a single block's execution, if it processes one token and immediately reloads x for output, L2 might still have it.\n\nFor best performance, explicitly keeping x in registers or SMEM is better.\n\nWith BLOCK_D = 4096 and num_threads = 256, we can just load x once into registers and keep it there for the output pass. 4096 bf16 = 8192 bytes. With 256 threads, each thread holds 32 bytes = 16 bf16 values. Triton's register allocator can handle this.\n\nLet me sketch this kernel:\n\n```python\n@triton.jit\ndef engram_gate_fwd_kernel(\n    hidden_states_ptr, k_ptr, v_ptr, weight_fused_ptr,\n    output_ptr, dot_ptr, gate_score_ptr, rstd_x_ptr, rstd_k_ptr,\n    num_tokens, hc_mult, hidden_size,\n    stride_xt, stride_xh, stride_xd,\n    stride_kt, stride_kh, stride_kd,\n    stride_vt, stride_vd,\n    stride_wt, stride_wd,\n    stride_ot, stride_oh, stride_od,\n    eps: tl.constexpr,\n    scalar: tl.constexpr,\n    clamp_value: tl.constexpr,\n    save_for_backward: tl.constexpr,\n    BLOCK_D: tl.constexpr,\n):\n    pid = tl.program_id(0)\n    num_programs = tl.num_programs(0)\n    total = num_tokens * hc_mult\n    \n    for idx in range(pid, total, num_programs):\n        t = idx // hc_mult\n        h = idx % hc_mult\n        \n        # Pointers\n        x_base = hidden_states_ptr + t * stride_xt + h * stride_xh\n        k_base = k_ptr + t * stride_kt + h * stride_kh\n        w_base = weight_fused_ptr + h * stride_wt\n        \n        sum_x2 = 0.0\n        sum_k2 = 0.0\n        sum_dot = 0.0\n        \n        # We can't easily keep the whole x in registers with a tile loop\n        # But if BLOCK_D == hidden_size, we do it in one shot\n        # Let's assert BLOCK_D == hidden_size for simplicity\n        \n        offs = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D)\n        \n        x = tl.load(x_base + offs * stride_xd).to(tl.float32)\n        k = tl.load(k_base + offs * stride_kd).to(tl.float32)\n        w = tl.load(w_base + offs * stride_wd)\n        \n        sum_x2 = tl.sum(x * x)\n        sum_k2 = tl.sum(k * k)\n        sum_dot = tl.sum(x * k * w)\n        \n        rstd_x_val = tl.rsqrt(sum_x2 / hidden_size + eps)\n        rstd_k_val = tl.rsqrt(sum_k2 / hidden_size + eps)\n        \n        dot_val = sum_dot * rstd_x_val * rstd_k_val * scalar\n        signed_sqrt = tl.copysign(tl.sqrt(tl.maximum(tl.abs(dot_val), clamp_value)), dot_val)\n        gate = tl.sigmoid(signed_sqrt)\n        \n        if save_for_backward:\n            # Only one thread should write\n            tl.store(dot_ptr + t * hc_mult + h, sum_dot)\n            tl.store(gate_score_ptr + t * hc_mult + h, gate)\n            tl.store(rstd_x_ptr + t * hc_mult + h, rstd_x_val)\n            tl.store(rstd_k_ptr + t * hc_mult + h, rstd_k_val)\n        \n        # Output\n        v_base = v_ptr + t * stride_vt\n        v = tl.load(v_base + offs * stride_vd).to(tl.float32)\n        out = x + gate * v\n        o_base = output_ptr + t * stride_ot + h * stride_oh\n        tl.store(o_base + offs * stride_od, out.to(tl.bfloat16))\n```\n\nWait, there are issues:\n1. `tl.copysign` - does Triton 3.6 support this? Let me check. Actually `tl.math.copysign` or `tl.copysign` should be available. Let me check if the hidden_size is always a multiple of some block size.\n\nLooking at the TileLang kernel, it asserts `hidden_size % blk_d == 0` and `hidden_size >= 2 * blk_d`. Or we can handle it with masks.\n\nActually, for the grader's benchmark size `hidden_size=4096`, we know exactly what to optimize for. For smaller hidden sizes in correctness tests, performance doesn't matter as much.\n\nLet me write a kernel that:\n1. Works for any hidden_size (with masks in loops)\n2. Is well-tuned for hidden_size=4096 and hc_mult=4\n\nFor hidden_size=4096, the ideal BLOCK_D might be 1024 or 2048 to fit well with Triton's tile size. Let me test both BLOCK_D=4096 and BLOCK_D=1024.\n\nActually, I realize there's another important factor: the shape of the tensors.\n- hidden_states: (num_tokens, hc_mult, hidden_size). Strides: for contiguous tensor, stride_xh = hidden_size, stride_xd = 1, stride_xt = hc_mult * hidden_size.\n- k: same shape as hidden_states. The TileLang kernel uses `k_stride_s, k_stride_h` indicating it might not be contiguous in the token dimension. We should handle strides.\n- v: (num_tokens, hidden_size). Strides: stride_vt = hidden_size, stride_vd = 1. Might not be contiguous in token dim.\n- weight_fused: (hc_mult, hidden_size). Stride_wt = hidden_size, stride_wd = 1.\n\nSo my kernel must use proper strides for all tensors.\n\nLet me draft the kernel more carefully. I'll use `tl.make_block_ptr` or explicit pointer arithmetic with strides.\n\nActually, for 1D access within the hidden_size dimension, pointer arithmetic is straightforward:\n```\nptr = base_ptr + t * stride_t + h * stride_h + d * stride_d\n```\nWith stride_d = 1 for all tensors.\n\nFor v, since it doesn't have a head dimension, the pointer is:\n```\nv_ptr + t * stride_vt + d * stride_vd\n```\n\nLet me write the kernel with explicit strides:\n\n```python\n@triton.jit\ndef engram_gate_fwd_kernel(\n    hidden_states_ptr, k_ptr, v_ptr, weight_fused_ptr,\n    output_ptr, dot_ptr, gate_score_ptr, rstd_x_ptr, rstd_k_ptr,\n    num_tokens, hc_mult, hidden_size,\n    stride_xt, stride_xh,\n    stride_kt, stride_kh,\n    stride_vt,\n    stride_wt,\n    stride_ot, stride_oh,\n    eps, scalar, clamp_value,\n    save_for_backward: tl.constexpr,\n    BLOCK_D: tl.constexpr,\n):\n    pid = tl.program_id(0)\n    num_programs = tl.num_programs(0)\n    total = num_tokens * hc_mult\n    \n    for idx in range(pid, total, num_programs):\n        t = idx // hc_mult\n        h = idx % hc_mult\n        \n        sum_x2 = 0.0\n        sum_k2 = 0.0\n        sum_dot = 0.0\n        \n        for d_start in range(0, hidden_size, BLOCK_D):\n            offs_d = d_start + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D)\n            mask = offs_d < hidden_size\n            \n            x_ptrs = hidden_states_ptr + t * stride_xt + h * stride_xh + offs_d\n            k_ptrs = k_ptr + t * stride_kt + h * stride_kh + offs_d\n            w_ptrs = weight_fused_ptr + h * stride_wt + offs_d\n            \n            x = tl.load(x_ptrs, mask=mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)\n            k = tl.load(k_ptrs, mask=mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)\n            w = tl.load(w_ptrs, mask=mask, other=0.0)\n            \n            sum_x2 += tl.sum(x * x)\n            sum_k2 += tl.sum(k * k)\n            sum_dot += tl.sum(x * k * w)\n        \n        rstd_x_val = tl.rsqrt(sum_x2 / hidden_size + eps)\n        rstd_k_val = tl.rsqrt(sum_k2 / hidden_size + eps)\n        \n        dot_val = sum_dot * rstd_x_val * rstd_k_val * scalar\n        abs_dot = tl.abs(dot_val)\n        clamped = tl.maximum(abs_dot, clamp_value)\n        signed_sqrt = (dot_val / tl.where(abs_dot == 0, 1.0, abs_dot)) * tl.sqrt(clamped)\n        # Or: signed_sqrt = tl.copysign(tl.sqrt(clamped), dot_val)\n        gate = tl.sigmoid(signed_sqrt)\n        \n        if save_for_backward:\n            tl.store(dot_ptr + t * hc_mult + h, sum_dot)\n            tl.store(gate_score_ptr + t * hc_mult + h, gate)\n            tl.store(rstd_x_ptr + t * hc_mult + h, rstd_x_val)\n            tl.store(rstd_k_ptr + t * hc_mult + h, rstd_k_val)\n        \n        for d_start in range(0, hidden_size, BLOCK_D):\n            offs_d = d_start + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D)\n            mask = offs_d < hidden_size\n            \n            x_ptrs = hidden_states_ptr + t * stride_xt + h * stride_xh + offs_d\n            v_ptrs = v_ptr + t * stride_vt + offs_d\n            o_ptrs = output_ptr + t * stride_ot + h * stride_oh + offs_d\n            \n            x = tl.load(x_ptrs, mask=mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)\n            v = tl.load(v_ptrs, mask=mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)\n            \n            out = x + gate * v\n            tl.store(o_ptrs, out.to(tl.bfloat16), mask=mask)\n```\n\nWait, this reloads x! That's bad for bandwidth. How can we avoid it?\n\nOption 1: Keep x in registers between reduction and output. But with the loop over BLOCK_D tiles, we'd need to store all tiles. We can't easily do this in Triton.\n\nOption 2: Use SMEM. We can load x and store it to a shared memory buffer, then read it back for output. Triton allows using shared memory explicitly?\n\nActually, yes! In Triton 3.x, we can declare shared memory using `tl.make_block_ptr` with explicit memory spaces, or we can simply use local arrays that the compiler promotes to SMEM.\n\nBut the simplest way is to structure the kernel so that we load x once and use it for both reduction and output:\n\n```python\nfor d_start in range(0, hidden_size, BLOCK_D):\n    offs_d = d_start + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D)\n    mask = offs_d < hidden_size\n    \n    x = tl.load(x_ptrs, mask=mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)\n    k = tl.load(k_ptrs, mask=mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)\n    w = tl.load(w_ptrs, mask=mask, other=0.0)\n    \n    sum_x2 += tl.sum(x * x)\n    sum_k2 += tl.sum(k * k)\n    sum_dot += tl.sum(x * k * w)\n    \n    # Store x in a local buffer for later? Not possible with block tensors across loop iterations...\n```\n\nActually, in Triton, block tensors are SSA (single static assignment). Within a loop, you can't accumulate arrays. The compiler transforms loops, but each tensor value is produced once.\n\nThis is a fundamental limitation. To keep x between reduction and output without reloading, we'd need to either:\n1. Not use a loop (BLOCK_D = hidden_size)\n2. Use SMEM explicitly\n\nFor option 1, if BLOCK_D = hidden_size = 4096:\n```python\noffs = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D)\nx = tl.load(x_ptrs, mask=mask).to(tl.float32)\n...\n# Now x is still in scope\nout = x + gate * v\ntl.store(o_ptrs, out.to(tl.bfloat16))\n```\n\nThis works! Since there's no loop over tiles, `x` remains in scope (either in registers or SMEM) and can be reused. The compiler will automatically handle where to keep it.\n\nSo the key insight is: **for hidden_size=4096, we should use BLOCK_D=4096 to avoid reloading x**. This saves 33% of memory bandwidth!\n\nWith BLOCK_D=4096, the memory traffic is:\nRead: x(256MB) + k(256MB) + v(64MB) + w(64KB) = 576 MB\nWrite: out(256MB) + intermediates(~1MB) = 257 MB\nTotal: ~833 MB\n\nAt 5.3 TB/s: ~0.157 ms\n\nIf we reload x (TileLang + our tiled version):\nRead: x(256MB) + k(256MB) + v(64MB) + w(64KB) + x_again(256MB) = 832 MB\nWrite: out(256MB) + intermediates = 257 MB\nTotal: ~1089 MB\nAt 5.3 TB/s: ~0.205 ms\n\nThe TileLang kernel avoids reloading x by keeping it in shared memory (`x_smem[hidden_size]`). So to match/be it, we need to do the same. The easiest way in Triton is BLOCK_D=4096.\n\nBut what if hidden_size is 7168? Then BLOCK_D=7168. Each thread handles 7168/256 = 28 elements. That's 56 bytes per thread. Still fine for registers. But 7168 bf16 = 14KB per tensor. With x, k, w loaded simultaneously = 42KB. Plus v for output. The compiler should handle this.\n\nHowever, Triton might have issues with very large block sizes. The contiguity analysis and vectorization might break or produce suboptimal code. But for powers of 2 and common sizes, it should work.\n\nLet me also think about BLOCK_D=4096 with different number of warps. With num_warps=4 (256 threads), each thread handles 16 bf16 = 32 bytes. With num_warps=2 (128 threads), each thread handles 32 bf16 = 64 bytes.\n\nOn AMD, I'd try num_warps=4 first.\n\nNow, one more thing: in the TileLang kernel, it uses `T.async_copy` and pipelining for k and v loads. For Triton, the compiler handles pipelining automatically through software pipelining passes. So we don't need to write explicit pipe stages.\n\nAnother optimization: instead of a for loop for persistent blocks, we might get better performance by launching exactly `num_tokens * hc_mult` blocks without persistence. This avoids the extra modulo/arithmetic in the loop and gives the hardware maximum scheduling flexibility.\n\nWith 32768 blocks and 256 CUs, each CU processes exactly 128 blocks. Since the blocks are independent and identical, the GPU scheduler should do a good job. The overhead of launching 32768 blocks is negligible on modern GPUs.\n\nActually, I wonder if a non-persistent 2D grid is better:\n```python\nnum_tokens, hc_mult, hidden_size = hidden_states.shape\ngrid = (num_tokens, hc_mult)\nkernel[grid](...)\n```\n\nBut wait, with a 2D grid, Triton uses `tl.program_id(0)` and `tl.program_id(1)`. The total number of blocks is 32768. This is fine.\n\nFor a persistent 1D grid, we might launch fewer blocks (e.g., 2048) and loop.\n```python\ngrid = (2048,)\nkernel[grid](...)\n```\n\nWhich is faster for 32768 tile instances on 256 CUs?\n\nFor memory bandwidth bound:\n- 2D grid of 32768 blocks: hardware serializes naturally. Very simple code. No loop overhead.\n- 1D grid of 2048 blocks with loop: each block does 16 iterations. Slightly more loop overhead, but better L2 locality because the block stays on the same CU.\n\nFor AMD MI350, I think the simple 2D grid is competitive and requires less tuning. But let me think about occupancy.\n\nWith a 2D grid of 32768 blocks, as blocks complete, new blocks are scheduled. Since each block only touches ~8KB of data (x tile + k tile + w tile), the L2 cache might not retain data for the next block. But consecutive blocks in the grid processing consecutive tokens might benefit from sequential access patterns.\n\nActually, with `grid=(num_tokens, hc_mult)`, consecutive `program_id(0)` values correspond to consecutive tokens for a given head. But when multiple blocks run in parallel, they could be at different tokens.\n\nWait, the memory access pattern for x is:\n- Token 0, Head 0: x[0, 0, 0:4096]\n- Token 0, Head 1: x[0, 1, 0:4096]\n- ...\n\nThese are contiguous within each head but strided between heads. The stride between head h and head h+1 is hidden_size. The stride between token t and token t+1 is hc_mult * hidden_size.\n\nSo for token t, all heads' data is at addresses offset by hidden_size from each other.\n\nFor v, it's (num_tokens, hidden_size), contiguous in hidden_size.\n\nThe TileLang kernel processes tokens persistently per head. That is, each block handles a range of tokens for a specific head. This means:\n- For head h, tokens t1..t2 are processed sequentially\n- k and x for these tokens are at `t * stride_t + h * hidden_size`\n- v for these tokens are at `t * stride_vt`\n\nSequential access in token dimension means consecutive memory addresses for each head. This is very L2 cache friendly.\n\nIn the 2D grid approach:\n- Block (t, h) processes token t, head h\n- Block (t+1, h) processes next token for same head\n- These might run on different SMs but the memory is sequential\n\nThe scheduling order of blocks in a 2D CUDA/ROCm grid is typically row-major. So block (0,0), (0,1), (0,2), (0,3), (1,0), (1,1), etc.\nThis means we process all 4 heads of token 0 first, then all 4 heads of token 1.\n\nMemory access pattern:\n- x[0,0,*], x[0,1,*], x[0,2,*], x[0,3,*] (interleaved with hidden_size stride)\n- x[1,0,*], x[1,1,*], ...\n\nThis alternates between heads quickly. For each head, the addresses are separated by hc_mult * hidden_size * 2 bytes = 4 * 4096 * 2 = 32KB.\n\nWith 32768 blocks, the scheduling might jump around a lot. But memory accesses are still within a 32KB stride, which is very L2-friendly.\n\nFor the persistent 1D grid approach with 2048 blocks:\n- Block 0 processes heads/tokens: (0,0), (2048,0), (4096,0), ...\n- Block 1 processes (0,1), (2048,1), (4096,1), ...\n- ...\n- Block 4 processes (1,0), (2049,0), ...\n\nIf we use `total = num_tokens * hc_mult` and `pid` is the block id:\n- `idx = pid + n * num_programs`\n- t = idx // hc_mult, h = idx % hc_mult\n\nWith num_programs=2048:\n- pid=0: (0,0), (512,0), (1024,0), ...\n- pid=1: (0,1), (512,1), ...\n- pid=4: (1,0), (512+1,0), ...\n\nWait, that's:\n- idx=0: t=0, h=0\n- idx=2048: t=512, h=0\n- idx=4096: t=1024, h=0\n\nFor block 0, it's processing every 512th token for head 0. On MI350 (gfx950?), HBM bandwidth is around 5-6 TB/s. For the target config: num_tokens=8192, hc=4, hidden=4096.\n\nReading hidden_states: 8192*4*4096*2 bytes = 268 MB\nReading k: 268 MB\nReading v: 8192*4096*2 = 67 MB\nReading weight_fused: 4*4096*4 = 64 KB (negligible)\nWriting output: 268 MB\nIf save_for_backward:\nWriting dot: 8192*4*4 = 128 KB\nWriting gate: 128 KB\nWriting rstd_x: 128 KB\nWriting rstd_k: 128 KB\n\nTotal memory traffic in save=True mode: read ~603 MB + write ~268.5 MB = ~872 MB. For Triton on ROCm, we might not have cp.async, so need to rely on good coalescing and block size choices.\n\nLet's think about the Triton kernel design:\n\nThe operation is per (token, head). Each token has hc_mult heads. hidden_size=4096.\n\nFor each (token, head):\n- Read x[hidden_size], k[hidden_size], v[hidden_size], w[hidden_size]\n- Compute sum(x^2), sum(k^2), sum(x * k * w)\n- Compute rstd_x = rsqrt(mean(x^2)+eps), rstd_k = rsqrt(mean(k^2)+eps)\n- dot = raw_dot * rstd_x * rstd_k * scalar\n- gate = sigmoid( sign(dot) * sqrt(max(|dot|, clamp_value)) )\n- out = x + gate * v\n\nv is shared across heads but each head writes its own output.\n\nThis is basically a variant of a gated linear unit with RMSNorm.\n\nSince it's per (token, head), we can launch one block per (token, head) or persistent style.\n\nMI350 has 256 CUs. Each CU can run multiple waves. Total work items = num_tokens * hc_mult = 32768. Using 1D blocks of threads per head: 32768 blocks. If block size = 128 threads: 32768 blocks. This is many waves. Persistent style is possible but Triton on AMD may not support it easily. Since the work is purely memory bound, maybe a simple 1D block per (token, head) with vectorized loads and stores is enough, provided we maximize thread occupancy and memory throughput.\n\nHowever, each block performs a reduction across hidden_size=4096 elements. With 128 threads, each thread handles 32 elements (if vec_size=1). If we use vec_size=4 (bfloat16 = 2 bytes, so 8 bytes per load), each thread handles 128 elements. 4096 / 128 = 32 iterations. That's fine.\n\nWait, each thread can load more. 128 threads * vec_size 8 * 4 bytes (float) = 4096 bytes per iteration. For bfloat16, vec_size=8 is 16 bytes per thread, 128*16=2048 bytes per iteration. 4096/ (128*8) = 4 iterations. Very few iterations. This is good.\n\nTo maximize bandwidth: use `tl.load` with `BLOCK_SIZE` such that each thread loads contiguous elements, and we do loop unrolling. For bfloat16, each element is 2 bytes.\n\nWe need to compute:\n- `sum_x2 = tl.sum(x * x)` where x is float.\n- `sum_k2 = tl.sum(k * k)`\n- `sum_xkw = tl.sum(x * k * w)`\n\nThen rstds, gate, then write `out = x + gate * v`.\n\nWe need to store `dot = raw_dot` (unscaled dot product), `gate_score`, `rstd_x`, `rstd_k` if `save_for_backward=True`.\n\nThe vectorized pattern in Triton: typically we define `BLOCK_SIZE` as the number of elements per thread? Actually in Triton, `tl.load` takes a pointer and a mask. We usually define one program per (token, head) and have each thread loop over `BLOCK_SIZE` elements.\n\nA standard approach:\n- Each program processes one (token, head).\n- `pid = tl.program_id(axis=0)` maps to `(token, head)`.\n- Within the program, we process `hidden_size` elements in chunks of `BLOCK_D`.\n- `BLOCK_D` could be e.g., 2048 or 4096.\n\nBut if `BLOCK_D = hidden_size`, then we can load the whole row in one go if we have enough threads. The max number of threads per block in Triton is typically 1024 (or more on MI350). 1024 threads * vec_size 8 = 8192 elements per block. `hidden_size=4096`, so we can fit in one block with 512 threads * vec_size 8 = 4096. But Triton prefers power-of-2 block sizes like 128, 256.\n\nWait, Triton block size refers to the number of elements in the dimension, not the number of threads. When we do `tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D)`, this creates a vector of `BLOCK_D` size. The compiler maps this to threads. If `BLOCK_D=4096`, it will use as many threads as needed (up to 1024) and loop.\n\nIn Triton, if we set `BLOCK_D=4096` and do one load of `[0:4096]`, the compiler will vectorize and coalesce automatically. But it may use a lot of registers.\n\nAlternatively, we can do `BLOCK_D=1024` and loop 4 times. With `num_warps=8` or `num_warps=4`.\n\nLet's think about the best Triton config for MI350.\n\nMI350 (CDNA3) has wavefront size 64 (unlike NVIDIA's 32). Triton on AMD should handle this. `num_warps=8` means 512 threads. With BLOCK_D=1024, each thread handles 2 elements. That's underutilized. With BLOCK_D=2048, 512 threads handle 4 elements each. With BLOCK_D=4096, 512 threads handle 8 elements each. This seems good.\n\nBut Triton kernel with `BLOCK_D=4096` and `num_warps=8` (512 threads) means the compiler needs to unroll 8 elements per thread. This is fine.\n\nHowever, we also have to load `v`. `v` is shared across heads. If each block loads `v`, that's `4096*2 = 8192 bytes` per block. With 32768 blocks, total `v` read traffic is 32768 * 8192 = 268 MB. That's correct. No duplication issue since each token is processed by 4 blocks (one per head). Each of the 4 blocks reads the same `v`. This is fine.\n\nBut there's a subtlety: if we have 32768 blocks, each reading 4 rows (x, k, w, v) of 4096 elements (bfloat16 except w is float32), the total memory traffic is high. To be precise:\n- x: bf16, 4096*2=8KB per block\n- k: bf16, 8KB\n- v: bf16, 8KB\n- w: fp32, 16KB\nTotal read per block: 40KB. For 32768 blocks: 1.28 GB. Wait, this is more than the theoretical minimum because:\n- x: 8192*4*4096*2 = 268MB\n- k: 268MB\n- v: 8192*4096*2 = 67MB\n- w: 4*4096*4 = 64KB\nTotal reads = ~603 MB. Writing output: 268MB. Total = 871MB.\nOur per-block calculation: 32768 * 40KB = 1.28 GB reads. That's higher! Why? Because w is float32: 16KB per block. 32768 * 16KB = 512 MB. weight_fused size is hc_mult * hidden_size * 4 = 4*4096*4 = 64 KB. Wait, each block reads the whole w row for its head. There are hc_mult=4 heads, and num_tokens=8192 tokens. So total w reads = num_tokens * hc_mult * hidden_size * 4 = 8192*4*4096*4 = 512 MB. Ah! The weight is float32. So reading it for every token is expensive, but necessary. Total reads: x (268MB) + k (268MB) + v (67MB) + w (512MB) = 1115 MB. Plus writes (268MB + 0.5MB) = ~1384 MB. At 5 TB/s, lower bound = 277 us. At 4 TB/s, 346 us. At 3 TB/s, 461 us. The TileLang kernel achieves ~610 us. So effective bandwidth of TileLang is 1384MB / 610us = 2.27 TB/s. Hmm, that seems low.\n\nWait, maybe my math is wrong. Let's recalculate:\n- x: (8192, 4, 4096) bf16 = 8192*4*4096*2 = 268,435,456 bytes = 256 MB\n- k: same = 256 MB\n- v: (8192, 4096) bf16 = 8192*4096*2 = 67,108,864 bytes = 64 MB\n- w: (4, 4096) fp32 = 4*4096*4 = 65,536 bytes = 64 KB\nTotal reads = 256 + 256 + 64 + 0.0625 = 576 MB.\nWait, w is only 64KB total, but it is read for every token? In HBM, caching in L2 might help. But L2 cache on MI350 is 16MB. The w tensor is tiny (64KB). It will be fully resident in L2 after the first few blocks. So the effective HBM traffic for w is negligible due to L2 cache. So effective reads from HBM are approximately x + k + v = 576 MB. Writes: output (256 MB) + intermediates (4 * 8192*4*4 = 0.5 MB) = 256.5 MB. Total HBM traffic = ~832.5 MB.\n\nAt 5 TB/s: 167 us. At 4 TB/s: 208 us. At 3 TB/s: 277 us. At 2 TB/s: 416 us.\nTileLang: 610 us -> effective bw = 832MB / 610us = 1.36 TB/s. That's quite low.\n\nWait, maybe TileLang reads v only once per token and writes output per head, but there might be other overhead. 610 us seems high. Let's check my benchmark. Maybe the first compile included. Re-run with more careful warmup and timing.\n\nActually, looking at the TileLang kernel: it uses shared memory to buffer x (bf16, 4096 elements = 8KB) and kv_smem (2 * blk_d bf16). With blk_d=1024, kv_smem is 4KB. So total smem ~12KB. This is small. It uses async_copy and pipelining. But maybe the persistent block logic adds some overhead.\n\nIf we can achieve ~200-250 us, we get the 2.5x speedup. That's a high bar but possible if we saturate HBM bandwidth better.\n\nLet's write a Triton kernel and see how it performs. A straightforward implementation:\n\n```python\nimport triton\nimport triton.language as tl\n\n@triton.jit\ndef engram_gate_fwd_kernel(\n    hidden_states_ptr, k_ptr, v_ptr, weight_fused_ptr, output_ptr,\n    dot_out_ptr, gate_score_ptr, rstd_x_ptr, rstd_k_ptr,\n    num_tokens, hc_mult, hidden_size,\n    eps, scalar, clamp_value,\n    save_for_backward: tl.constexpr,\n    BLOCK_D: tl.constexpr,\n):\n    pid = tl.program_id(0)\n    token = pid // hc_mult\n    head = pid % hc_mult\n    \n    if token >= num_tokens:\n        return\n    \n    # base pointers\n    x_ptr = hidden_states_ptr + (token * hc_mult + head) * hidden_size\n    k_ptr_head = k_ptr + (token * hc_mult + head) * hidden_size\n    w_ptr = weight_fused_ptr + head * hidden_size\n    v_ptr_token = v_ptr + token * hidden_size\n    out_ptr = output_ptr + (token * hc_mult + head) * hidden_size\n    \n    # Can I keep them in shared memory or registers?\n\nFor BLOCK_SIZE=4096 and 256 threads:\n- x: 4096 * 2 bytes = 8 KB\n- k: 8 KB\n- v: 8 KB\n- w: 4096 * 4 bytes = 16 KB\nTotal SMEM: ~40 KB, which fits easily in the 228 KB per CU on MI350.\n\nSo we could load x, k, w into shared memory in the first pass, then reuse them in the second pass. This would halve the memory traffic for x and k.\n\nBut for save_for_backward=False, the total traffic would be:\n- Read x: 256 MB\n- Read k: 256 MB\n- Read v: 64 MB\n- Read w: 64 KB\n- Write out: 256 MB\nTotal: ~832 MB\n\nWith two passes (no shared memory caching): read x twice (512 MB), read k twice (512 MB), read v once (64 MB), write out (256 MB) = 1344 MB.\nWith shared memory: read x once (256 MB), read k once (256 MB), read v once (64 MB), write out (256 MB) = 832 MB.\n\nSo caching in shared memory saves 512 MB of reads! This is a big deal.\n\nBut there's a catch: with 32768 blocks and 256 CUs, at any given time only ~256 blocks are running (one per CU, assuming one block per CU). Each block uses 40 KB SMEM. Total SMEM used: 256 * 40 KB = 10 MB. The MI350 has much more SMEM than this, so we could potentially run multiple blocks per CU.\n\nActually, MI350 has 64 KB per SIMD (wave), or 128 KB per CU? Let me check.\n\nActually, I don't know the exact SMEM per CU for this GPU, but 40 KB should be well within limits.\n\nWait, the TileLang kernel already does this! Looking at the TileLang kernel:\n```python\nx_smem = T.alloc_shared((hidden_size,), T.bfloat16)      # 8 KB\nkv_smem = T.alloc_shared((2, blk_d), T.bfloat16)          # 2 * blk_d * 2 bytes\n```\n\nAnd it keeps x in x_smem across both passes. Or maybe I can use larger blocks and more warps.\n\nActually, let me look more carefully at the TileLang kernel. It uses `blk_d = _choose_blk_d(hidden_size)` which for hidden_size=4096 would be 1024 (since 4096 % 1024 == 0 and 4096 >= 2048). Then `num_blk = 4096 / 1024 = 4`.\n\nSo TileLang processes the hidden dimension in 4 tiles of 1024 elements each, with a 2-phase double buffer for k/v in shared memory. This means it needs to do 4 iterations of cp.async and synchronization.\n\nIf I process the entire hidden_size=4096 in one tile with 256 threads, each thread handles 16 elements. This eliminates the loop overhead and syncs.\n\nBut can I fit everything in shared memory?\n- x: 4096 * 2 = 8192 bytes\n- k: 4096 * 2 = 8192 bytes  \n- v: 4096 * 2 = 8192 bytes\n- w: 4096 * 4 = 16384 bytes\nTotal: 40960 bytes\n\nIf we have 64 KB per CU, we can fit this easily and still run one block per CU. If we have 128 KB per CU, we might run 2-3 blocks per CU.\n\nActually, a better approach: don't even use shared memory for everything. Just load directly into registers. Each thread handles 16 elements:\n- x_local: 16 floats = 64 bytes\n- k_local: 64 bytes\n- w_local: 64 bytes\n- v_local: 64 bytes\nTotal registers per thread: ~256 bytes = 64 KB per block (256 threads). This is very reasonable.\n\nWith registers, we avoid shared memory bank conflicts and the compiler handles everything optimally. We load x, k, w once into registers for the reduction, then retain the gate scalar and load v into registers for the output write.\n\nWait, but we need to write x + gate * v. If we don't store x in registers or shared memory between passes, we have to reload x. Can we keep x in registers?\n\nIf each thread processes 16 contiguous elements:\n- Load x[0:16], k[0:16], w[0:16] into registers\n- Compute partial sums: sum_x2, sum_k2, sum_xkw\n- After reduction across threads, compute gate\n- Load v[0:16] into registers\n- Compute out = x + gate * v (using the original x registers)\n- Write out\n\nThis only requires ONE pass over HBM for x, k, and w, and one pass for v! Total memory traffic is minimized.\n\nBut there's a problem: the reductions (sum_x2, sum_k2, sum_xkw) need to be computed across all elements before we know gate. If each thread computes partial sums for its 16 elements, then does a block-level reduction (warp shuffle or shared memory), then computes gate, then writes output. This works!\n\nThe key is that we can keep x in registers after computing the partial sums. Since the partial sums are scalars, we don't need to store x anywhere. We just keep x_local, k_local, w_local in registers, compute partial sums, sync/reduce, compute gate, load v, compute output.\n\nBut wait - how do we load v? v is per-token, shared across heads. If each block handles one (token, head), we still need to load v. We can load v after computing gate.\n\nLet me write this out more clearly:\n\n```python\n@triton.jit\ndef engram_gate_fwd_kernel(\n    hidden_states_ptr, k_ptr, v_ptr, weight_fused_ptr, output_ptr,\n    dot_ptr, gate_score_ptr, rstd_x_ptr, rstd_k_ptr,\n    num_tokens, hc_mult, hidden_size,\n    eps, clamp_value, scalar,\n    save_for_backward: tl.constexpr,\n    BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,\n):\n    pid = tl.program_id(0)\n    token_idx = pid // hc_mult\n    head_idx = pid % hc_mult\n    \n    if token_idx >= num_tokens:\n        return\n    \n    # Offsets\n    x_base = hidden_states_ptr + (token_idx * hc_mult + head_idx) * hidden_size\n    k_base = k_ptr + (token_idx * hc_mult + head_idx) * hidden_size\n    v_base = v_ptr + token_idx * hidden_size\n    w_base = weight_fused_ptr + head_idx * hidden_size\n    out_base = output_ptr + (token_idx * hc_mult + head_idx) * hidden_size\n    \n    offsets = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)\n    mask = offsets < hidden_size\n    \n    # Load x, k, w (one-shot if BLOCK_SIZE == hidden_size)\n    x = tl.load(x_base + offsets, mask=mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)\n    k_val = tl.load(k_base + offsets, mask=mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)\n    w = tl.load(w_base + offsets, mask=mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)\n    \n    # Compute partial sums\n    sum_x2 = tl.sum(x * x, axis=0)\n    sum_k2 = tl.sum(k_val * k_val, axis=0)\n    sum_xkw = tl.sum(x * k_val * w, axis=0)\n    \n    # Compute scalars\n    rstd_x_val = tl.libdevice.rsqrt(sum_x2 / hidden_size + eps)\n    rstd_k_val = tl.libdevice.rsqrt(sum_k2 / hidden_size + eps)\n    \n    dot_scaled = sum_xkw * rstd_x_val * rstd_k_val * scalar\n    abs_dot = tl.abs(dot_scaled)\n    clamped = tl.maximum(abs_dot, clamp_value)\n    signed_sqrt = tl.where(dot_scaled >= 0, tl.sqrt(clamped), -tl.sqrt(clamped))\n    gate = tl.sigmoid(signed_sqrt)\n    \n    if save_for_backward:\n        tl.store(dot_ptr + token_idx * hc_mult + head_idx, sum_xkw)\n        tl.store(gate_score_ptr + token_idx * hc_mult + head_idx, gate)\n        tl.store(rstd_x_ptr + token_idx * hc_mult + head_idx, rstd_x_val)\n        tl.store(rstd_k_ptr + token_idx * hc_mult + head_idx, rstd_k_val)\n    \n    # Load v and compute output\n    v_val = tl.load(v_base + offsets, mask=mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)\n    out = x + gate * v_val\n    tl.store(out_base + offsets, out.to(tl.bfloat16), mask=mask)\n```\n\nWait, but BLOCK_SIZE can't necessarily equal hidden_size in Triton. Usually `tl.load` with block of size `[BLOCK_SIZE]` where BLOCK_SIZE = e.g. 256 and each thread handles 8 elements. But Triton vectorization is implicit. We can use `tl.load(ptrs, mask=mask)` and Triton will vectorize.\n\nHowever, Triton kernels for reduction often look like:\n```\nfor off in range(0, BLOCK_SIZE, BLOCK_N):\n    x = tl.load(x_ptr + off)\n    ...\n```\nand we use `tl.sum` across the BLOCK_SIZE dimension. But Triton on AMD often uses 64 threads per warp.\n`num_warps`: On AMD, `num_warps=1` means 64 threads. `num_warps=2` means 128 threads, etc.\nWait, Triton on AMD: `num_warps` refers to wavefronts. A wavefront is 64 threads.\nSo `num_warps=4` is 256 threads. `num_warps=8` is 512 threads.\nTo load 4096 elements with 512 threads, each thread loads 8 elements (128-bit vector). This is perfect vectorization.\nLet's check: num_warps=8 threads=512. Hidden_size=4096. 4096/512 = 8. So each thread handles 8 bf16 elements. Vector size 8 (128-bit) is ideal.\nFor hidden_size=7168, 7168/512 = 14. That's not a power of 2, but 14 elements per thread. 14*2=28 bytes per thread. Not ideal for vectorization? We can vectorize by 8 and do 1 loop + 6 extra? Or vectorize by 4 and do 3 loops + 2 extra?\nBetter to loop with a vectorized load inside.\n\nSo let's design a kernel:\n```python\n@triton.jit\ndef engram_gate_fwd_kernel(\n    hidden_states_ptr, k_ptr, v_ptr, weight_fused_ptr, output_ptr,\n    dot_ptr, gate_score_ptr, rstd_x_ptr, rstd_k_ptr,\n    num_tokens, hc_mult, hidden_size,\n    eps, clamp_value, scalar,\n    save_for_backward: tl.constexpr,\n    BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,\n):\n    pid = tl.program_id(0)\n    token_id = pid // hc_mult\n    head_id = pid % hc_mult\n    \n    # Offsets for this token-head\n    base_x = (token_id * hc_mult + head_id) * hidden_size\n    base_k = base_x  # same shape as x\n    base_w = head_id * hidden_size\n    base_v = token_id * hidden_size\n    \n    # Thread-local accumulators\n    acc_x_sq = 0.0\n    acc_k_sq = 0.0\n    acc_dot = 0.0\n    \n    # Process hidden dimension in chunks of BLOCK_SIZE\n    for start in range(0, hidden_size, BLOCK_SIZE):\n        offsets = start + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)\n        mask = offsets < hidden_size\n        \n        x = tl.load(hidden_states_ptr + base_x + offsets, mask=mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)\n        k = tl.load(k_ptr + base_k + offsets, mask=mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)\n        w = tl.load(weight_fused_ptr + base_w + offsets, mask=mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)\n        \n        acc_x_sq += tl.sum(x * x)\n        acc_k_sq += tl.sum(k * k)\n        acc_dot += tl.sum(x * k * w)\n    \n    # Compute rstds and gate\n    rstd_x_val = tl.rsqrt(acc_x_sq / hidden_size + eps)\n    rstd_k_val = tl.rsqrt(acc_k_sq / hidden_size + eps)\n    \n    dot_val = acc_dot * rstd_x_val * rstd_k_val * scalar\n    # sign(dot) * sqrt(max(abs(dot), clamp_value))\n    signed_sqrt = tl.where(dot_val >= 0, 1.0, -1.0) * tl.sqrt(tl.maximum(tl.abs(dot_val), clamp_value))\n    gate_val = tl.sigmoid(signed_sqrt)\n    \n    if save_for_backward:\n        tl.store(dot_ptr + token_id * hc_mult + head_id, acc_dot)\n        tl.store(gate_score_ptr + token_id * hc_mult + head_id, gate_val)\n        tl.store(rstd_x_ptr + token_id * hc_mult + head_id, rstd_x_val)\n        tl.store(rstd_k_ptr + token_id * hc_mult + head_id, rstd_k_val)\n    \n    # Second pass: compute output = x + gate * v\n    for start in range(0, hidden_size, BLOCK_SIZE):\n        offsets = start + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)\n        mask = offsets < hidden_size\n        \n        x = tl.load(hidden_states_ptr + base_x + offsets, mask=mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)\n        v = tl.load(v_ptr + base_v + offsets, mask=mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)\n        \n        out = x + gate_val * v\n        tl.store(output_ptr + base_x + offsets, out.to(tl.bfloat16), mask=mask)\n```\n\nWait, but this reads `x` twice and reads `v` once but only for this head. `v` is the same across heads.\nTotal memory reads per block: x (2*D), k (2*D), w (4*D) in pass 1; x (2*D), v (2*D) in pass 2.\nTotal: 2+2+4 + 2+2 = 12*D bytes. Plus writes: 2*D + 4*4 = 2D+16 bytes.\nFor D=4096: 12*4096 = 49152 bytes read per block.\nWith 32768 blocks, total read = 1.5 GB. Write = 0.25 GB + negligible. If the theoretical max is ~5.3TB/s, then at 1.75GB, the minimum time is ~330us.\nSo 609us means it's achieving ~2.9 TB/s. Getting to ~240us means 7.3 TB/s, impossible.\nWAIT. Let me re-read the performance metric.\n\"your kernel must be at least 60% faster than the TileLang kernel (i.e. TileLang_latency / your_latency ≥ 2.5, equivalently your latency ≤ 40% of TileLang's)\"\n\nWait. `TileLang_latency / your_latency ≥ 2.5`.\nIf TileLang is 609us, then my latency must be ≤ 609/2.5 = 243.6 us.\nBut theoretical minimum at peak bandwidth (~5.3TB/s) for 1.75GB is 330us.\nThis is a contradiction.\n\nLet me re-calculate the bytes.\n`num_tokens=8192, hc_mult=4, hidden_size=4096`.\nInputs: x = 8192 * 4 * 4096 * 2 = 268,435,456 bytes = 256 MB.\nk = 256 MB.\nv = 8192 * 4096 * 2 = 64 MB.\nw_fused = 4 * 4096 * 4 = 64 KB (negligible, cached? But counts as read).\nOutputs: out = 256 MB.\ndot = 8192 * 4 * 4 = 128 KB.\ngate_score = 128 KB.\nrstd_x = 128 KB.\nrstd_k = 128 KB.\n\nTotal memory traffic:\nRead: x(256MB) + k(256MB) + v(64MB) + w(64KB) = 576 MB.\nWrite: out(256MB) + dot(128KB) + gate(128KB) + rstd_x(128KB) + rstd_k(128KB) = 256.5 MB.\nTotal: ~832.5 MB.\n\nWait, if we read x twice, that's 512MB. If we read k once (256MB), v once (64MB), w once (64KB).\nTotal read = 832MB. Write = 256.5MB. Total = 1088.5 MB.\nAt 5.3 TB/s = 5.3e12 B/s. Time = 1.0885e9 / 5.3e12 = 205 us.\nAh! So theoretical minimum is around 205us.\nIf TileLang takes 609us, it's at ~1.8 TB/s. That makes sense if it's inefficient on MI350.\nThen 243us target is achievable at ~4.5 TB/s, which is ~85% of peak. That is achievable with a very optimized kernel.\n\nWait, but reading x twice (in two passes) is already 512MB. Can we avoid reading x twice?\nIn the TileLang kernel, x is loaded into shared memory in pass 1, and reused from shared memory in pass 2.\nBut shared memory size is limited. `hidden_size * 2` bytes = 8KB for 4096. This is a huge waste on AMD.\nThis explains why the kernel is so slow on MI350.\n\nA Triton kernel should fix this by using AMD-appropriate configurations: full wavefronts (64 threads), coalesced vectorized loads, minimal shared memory usage.\n\nCan we write a single-pass kernel where x is read once and kept in registers?\nIf BLOCK_SIZE = hidden_size, then we can load the entire x, k, w, v into registers for each thread.\nFor hidden_size=4096: with 512 threads (num_warps=8), each thread handles 8 elements.\n8 bf16 = 16 bytes. Let's think.\nThe TileLang kernel launches `hc_mult * num_persistent_blocks` blocks.\n`num_persistent_blocks = num_sms * blocks_per_sm // hc_mult`.\nFor hidden_size=4096, `blk_d=1024` (or 512). `smem_bytes = hidden_size * 2 + blk_d * 4 = 8192 + 4096 = 12288` bytes.\n`blocks_per_sm = min(128KB // 12288, 16) = min(10, 16) = 10`.\n`num_persistent_blocks = 256 * 10 // 4 = 640`.\nTotal blocks = `4 * 640 = 2560`.\nWait, 2560 blocks total? Each CU gets 5 wavefronts. That's very low occupancy. CU can hold many more.\nIf each CU can hold say 40 wavefronts, we are severely underutilizing the CUs.\nThis explains the low bandwidth: terrible occupancy due to small thread count per block and persistent blocks limiting total parallelism.\nAdditionally, using only 32 threads per block means the memory coalescing width is only 32 threads on NVIDIA (warp), but on AMD a wavefront is 64 threads. If only 32 threads are active in a block, the other 32 threads in the wavefront execute nothing, and memory loads might be less efficient.\n\nSo the key to beating TileLang by 2.5x is to use many more threads per block and not use persistent kernels (let Triton handle block scheduling).\nWith `(num_tokens * hc_mult)` blocks = 32768 blocks, and 512 threads per block (8 warps), total threads = 16.7M.\nTotal wavefronts = 16.7M / 64 = 262k wavefronts.\n256 CUs * ~40 wavefronts/CU = ~10k wavefronts can be resident. So there are many waves to keep the CUs busy.\nThis will saturate memory bandwidth much better.\n\nSo the strategy is:\n1. Use a Triton kernel with many threads per block. Target 512 threads (num_warps=8 on AMD).\n2. Launch `(num_tokens * hc_mult)` blocks, one per token-head.\n3. Use a single-pass approach if possible to minimize reads.\n   But Triton can't easily keep the whole x in registers/SMEM without two passes.\n   However, 2-pass with good occupancy might still be enough.\n   Let's calculate: 2-pass = 1088MB total traffic. At 4.5TB/s = 242us.\n   1-pass (using SMEM to store x) = 832MB total traffic. At 4.0TB/s = 208us.\n   1-pass might be safer for meeting the target.\n   But can we do 1-pass in Triton?\n\nWait! Triton does support `tl.load` and then we can just keep the variable in a register. The issue is if the block processes a PART of hidden_size (loops), it can't keep all parts.\nWhat if we process the ENTIRE hidden_size in one block?\nFor hidden_size=4096, BLOCK_SIZE=4096.\nNum threads: let's use num_warps=8 (512 threads).\nEach thread handles 4096/512 = 8 elements.\n`x = tl.load(..., block_shape=(4096,))` results in a block tensor of shape (4096,).\nEach thread gets 8 elements.\nWe can compute `acc_x_sq = tl.sum(x * x)`. `acc_k_sq = tl.sum(k * k)`. `acc_dot = tl.sum(x * k * w)`.\nThen compute gate.\nThen `out = x + gate * v`.\nThen `tl.store(output_ptr + ..., out.to(tl.bfloat16))`.\nHere, `x` is loaded once and kept in registers through to the output store! `v` is loaded once.\nThis is a true single-pass kernel!\nTotal memory traffic: read x(256MB) + k(256MB) + v(64MB) + w(64KB) + write out(256MB) + intermediates(0.5MB).\nTotal = ~832.5 MB.\nAt 4.5 TB/s = 185us.\nThis is well under the 243us target.\n\nCan Triton handle BLOCK_SIZE=4096 with num_warps=8?\nYes, `tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)` generates a vector of 4096 values.\nThe compiler will distribute it across threads.\nEach thread will have 8 elements in registers.\n`x * x`, `x * k * w` are register-to-register operations.\n`tl.sum` does a tree reduction across threads.\nThen `x + gate * v` is element-wise.\nThis is very efficient.\n\nWhat about hidden_size=7168?\nBLOCK_SIZE=7168. num_warps=8 -> 512 threads. The block launch overhead is minimal.\nThe memory bandwidth might not saturate as well because the workload per block is tiny, but with so many blocks (32768), it should still be okay. 32768 blocks with 512 threads = 16M threads. That's a lot.\n\nLet's test with a simple kernel.\nActually, I should write the kernel and benchmark it.\n\nWait, `tl.rsqrt` is available in Triton.\n`tl.sqrt` is available.\n`tl.abs` is available.\n`tl.sigmoid` is available.\n`tl.maximum` is available.\n`tl.where` is available.\n\nThere's no `tl.copysign` but we can emulate with `tl.where` as I showed.\nOr even simpler: `signed_sqrt = tl.sign(dot_val) * tl.sqrt(tl.maximum(tl.abs(dot_val), clamp_value))`.\nIs `tl.sign` available? Or maybe `math.copysign`?\nEarlier I saw `copysign` is False. So we use `tl.where(dot_val >= 0, 1.0, -1.0)`.\nNote: need to handle `dot_val == 0`. The sign of 0 doesn't matter much here because sqrt(0) = 0, and sigmoid(0) = 0.5. If we return -1 for 0, signed_sqrt is -0, which is still 0.\nSo `tl.where(dot_val >= 0, 1.0, -1.0)` is fine.\n\nNow, about the function signature:\n```python\ndef engram_gate_fwd_triton(\n    hidden_states: torch.Tensor,   # (num_tokens, hc_mult, hidden_size), bfloat16\n    k: torch.Tensor,               # (num_tokens, hc_mult, hidden_size), bfloat16\n    v: torch.Tensor,               # (num_tokens, hidden_size), bfloat16\n    weight_fused: torch.Tensor,    # (hc_mult, hidden_size), float32  (= weight_hidden * weight_embed)\n    eps: float,\n    clamp_value: float,\n    save_for_backward: bool = True,\n):\n```\nIt returns `(output, dot, gate_score, rstd_x, rstd_k)`.\n`dot` is `raw_dot` (unscaled dot product), float32, shape (num_tokens, hc_mult).\n`gate_score` is float32, shape (num_tokens, hc_mult).\n`rstd_x`, `rstd_k` are float32, shape (num_tokens, hc_mult).\n`output` is bfloat16, shape (num_tokens, hc_mult, hidden_size).\n\nImportant: When `save_for_backward=False`, only `output` is required to be correct. Others must be `None`.\n\nThe inputs might not be contiguous in the last dimension? The problem says `k.stride(-1)==1` and `v.stride(-1)==1` in TileLang.\nWe should probably assert or handle strides.\n`hidden_states` might be contiguous. The shapes are standard.\nFor simplicity, I'll assume standard strides: `hidden_states` has stride `(hc_mult * hidden_size, hidden_size, 1)`. `k` might have different strides for the first two dims.\n`v` has stride `(hidden_size, 1)`.\n`weight_fused` has stride `(hidden_size, 1)`.\n\nIn Triton kernel, we can pass base pointers and strides.\n\nLet's write the Triton kernel.\n\n```python\nimport torch\nimport triton\nimport triton.language as tl\n\n@triton.jit\ndef _engram_gate_fwd_kernel(\n    x_ptr,\n    k_ptr,\n    v_ptr,\n    w_ptr,\n    out_ptr,\n    dot_ptr,\n    gate_ptr,\n    rstd_x_ptr,\n    rstd_k_ptr,\n    stride_x_t,\n    stride_x_h,\n    stride_x_d,\n    stride_k_t,\n    stride_k_h,\n    stride_k_d,\n    stride_v_t,\n    stride_v_d,\n    stride_w_h,\n    stride_w_d,\n    num_tokens,\n    hc_mult,\n    hidden_size,\n    eps,\n    clamp_value,\n    scalar,\n    save_for_backward: tl.constexpr,\n    BLOCK_SIZE: tl.constexpr,\n):\n    pid = tl.program_id(0)\n    token_id = pid // hc_mult\n    head_id = pid % hc_mult\n    \n    if token_id >= num_tokens:\n        return\n    \n    # Compute base offsets\n    x_base = x_ptr + token_id * stride_x_t + head_id * stride_x_h\n    k_base = k_ptr + token_id * stride_k_t + head_id * stride_k_h\n    v_base = v_ptr + token_id * stride_v_t\n    w_base = w_ptr + head_id * stride_w_h\n    out_base = out_ptr + token_id * stride_x_t + head_id * stride_x_h  # same as x\n    \n    # Reduction phase\n    acc_x_sq = 0.0\n    acc_k_sq = 0.0\n    acc_dot = 0.0\n    \n    for off in range(0, hidden_size, BLOCK_SIZE):\n        offsets = off + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)\n        mask = offsets < hidden_size\n        \n        x = tl.load(x_base + offsets * stride_x_d, mask=mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)\n        k = tl.load(k_base + offsets * stride_k_d, mask=mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)\n        w = tl.load(w_base + offsets * stride_w_d, mask=mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)\n        \n        acc_x_sq += tl.sum(x * x, axis=0)\n        acc_k_sq += tl.sum(k * k, axis=0)\n        acc_dot += tl.sum(x * k * w, axis=0)\n    \n    rstd_x_val = tl.rsqrt(acc_x_sq / hidden_size + eps)\n    rstd_k_val = tl.rsqrt(acc_k_sq / hidden_size + eps)\n    \n    dot_val = acc_dot * rstd_x_val * rstd_k_val * scalar\n    signed_sqrt = tl.where(dot_val >= 0, 1.0, -1.0) * tl.sqrt(tl.maximum(tl.abs(dot_val), clamp_value))\n    gate_val = tl.sigmoid(signed_sqrt)\n    \n    if save_for_backward:\n        out_idx = token_id * hc_mult + head_id\n        tl.store(dot_ptr + out_idx, acc_dot)\n        tl.store(gate_ptr + out_idx, gate_val)\n        tl.store(rstd_x_ptr + out_idx, rstd_x_val)\n        tl.store(rstd_k_ptr + out_idx, rstd_k_val)\n    \n    # Output phase\n    for off in range(0, hidden_size, BLOCK_SIZE):\n        offsets = off + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)\n        mask = offsets < hidden_size\n        \n        x = tl.load(x_base + offsets * stride_x_d, mask=mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)\n        v = tl.load(v_base + offsets * stride_v_d, mask=mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)\n        \n        out = x + gate_val * v\n        tl.store(out_base + offsets * stride_x_d, out.to(tl.bfloat16), mask=mask)\n```\n\nWait, is `stride_x_d` always 1? Probably. But to be safe, I'll use strides.\nActually, `tl.load(ptr + offsets * stride)` might prevent vectorization if stride is not 1 or if the compiler can't prove contiguous access.\nTo maximize performance, we should ensure we use `tl.load(base_ptr + offsets)` where `offsets` is `tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE)` and the base pointer is already aligned to the start of the contiguous dimension.\nSo `x_base` should be `x_ptr + token_id * stride_x_t + head_id * stride_x_h`, and then load `x_base + offsets` assuming `stride_x_d == 1`.\nIf `stride_x_d != 1`, this might be a problem, but typically the last dim is contiguous.\nSame for other tensors.\nLet me check the test data generation: `torch.randn(..., device='cuda')` creates contiguous tensors by default.\nIn the actual model, these might be contiguous too. So total VGPR storage is 256 * 64 * 4 bytes = 64KB per SIMD.\n   With 4 SIMDs per CU, total 256KB vector register file per CU.\n   Triton usually generates LLVM IR and the backend handles register allocation.\n   If we load 8 elements, that's 8 float32 values (for computation). So one VGPR can hold one 32-bit value for all 64 threads. So 256 VGPRs means 256 32-bit values per thread.\n   Ah! I see. So each thread in the wavefront gets 256 VGPRs (64-lane wide).
